The file's caution — recorded here in the asset section because it belongs to the honest accounting of strengths — is that several of these assets are *paired* with the liabilities documented elsewhere. The sublimation that produces is the sublimation that suppresses. The counterphobic courage that saves lives is the counterphobic courage that selects the wrong cases. The prosthetic integration that grants psychological wholeness is the prosthetic integration that obviates the grieving the body still owes. The handler role that fits is the handler role that armors.

She is, on the asset side of the ledger, formidable, and on the asset side of the ledger she is most accurately understood as *formidable in the present tense, with a deferred bill*. The file recommends that she be valued, supported, and — when she will allow it, which will be rarely and only through Colleen — *cared for*, on the understanding that the strengths are genuine and the strengths are not free.

— END SECTION —


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION — KNIGHT, MERCEDES

## Preamble: What "Breaking" Means For This Subject

The subject does not break the way most operators break. She does not flame out mid-mission, she does not freeze under fire, she does not develop a tremor in the trigger finger or refuse the call. Her defensive architecture is too well-machined for any of those classical presentations. What she does instead is **complete the job and then absent herself** — geographically, emotionally, or chemically — for a period that scales with the magnitude of what she just absorbed. The decompensation is **post-operational, private, and time-shifted**. By the time anyone close to her notices something is wrong, the wrong thing has already been wrong for weeks. This is the single most important clinical fact about her failure profile: **she is a delayed-onset decompensator, and the delay is itself part of the pathology.**

The corollary, which any handler running her must internalize: **she will never tell you she is breaking**. She will tell you she is tired. She will tell you the case ran long. She will tell you she's just going to "take a couple days." She will tell you Colleen needs her in the office. The verbal channel is not an instrument the truth travels on when the truth concerns her own interior. Watch the somatic and logistical channels — they are unguarded because she does not believe they communicate.

---

## The Escalation Ladder, Stage by Stage

### Stage 0 — Baseline (Operational Steady State)

Working two to four cases at staggered intensities. Sleeping five to six hours, broken once, gun within arm's reach on the nightstand on the prosthetic side (she draws cross-body with the organic hand because the bionic is too forceful for trigger control under hypnopompic confusion). Coffee from the same Harlem bodega, two cups before the office, a third by mid-morning. Banter with Colleen is at full register — quick, layered, mutually disrespectful in the affectionate mode. Romantic partner, if currently present, gets evenings two or three nights a week. Drinking is social: bourbon, neat, two glasses, occasionally three. Eats irregularly but eats. Hair maintained on a roughly six-week cycle. Visits the gym for sparring twice a week; runs the prosthetic through its calibration paces (squeeze cycles, range-of-motion sweeps) in the bathroom mirror most mornings — a ritual she performs without acknowledging it as ritual.

This is the floor. Everything below is degradation from here.

### Stage 1 — Compressive Loading (mild stress / case complexity rising)

The first observable shift is **verbal**. The wisecracks get faster, sharper, and more frequent. The proportion of her speech that is barbed deflection rises from a baseline of perhaps fifteen percent to thirty, then forty. Colleen notices first and does not say so; she matches the cadence and waits. The second shift is **caffeine load** — the third cup becomes a fourth, and a fifth appears in the late afternoon. The third shift is **schedule compression**: she stops eating lunch, eats dinner at her desk, stays at the office past midnight on case nights. The fourth shift, almost invisible, is **prosthetic fidgeting** — she begins running the calibration sweeps not just morning but at intervals through the day, idle squeeze cycles while reading a file, full rotation checks at the desk. The arm is being asked to absorb stress the rest of her is generating, and she is, without conscious intent, consulting it for reassurance.

Romantic partner contact thins. Texts get shorter. She does not cancel dates so much as let them shift to the margins of the week. Sex, when it occurs, is initiated by her and is more physical and less talked through than at baseline — a discharge channel, not a connection channel. She sleeps the same hours but worse.

She is fully functional at this stage and would describe herself as fine, with mild irritation that the question was asked.

### Stage 2 — Defensive Hardening (moderate stress / loss of operational tempo OR a partner-side crisis)

The verbal register narrows. The barbs are still there but the warmth thins out underneath them; Colleen feels the difference before she can articulate it — the jokes have started landing without the smile behind them. She becomes **terse with everyone except Colleen and clients**, and the deference to clients is performative, a professional mask. She stops returning non-essential calls. The romantic partner, if extant, receives fewer touches in passing; she stops reaching for him in the kitchen, stops the small unconscious physical accountings she does at baseline (hand on shoulder when stepping past, knee against his under the table).

Drinking moves: she still drinks socially but now also drinks alone. Not heavily — a single bourbon in the kitchen at one in the morning, lights off, looking at the window. This is the most diagnostic single image in her decompensation pattern and almost no one in her life has ever seen it.

The prosthetic gets harder use. She begins favoring it for tasks where the organic arm would do — opening doors, lifting weighted objects, gripping subjects in interrogation. This produces a postural shift: a slight rightward lean, the right shoulder carried lower and more forward than the left. Anyone trained to read bodies sees it across a room. She does not feel it. The compensatory left-side strain (cervical, mid-thoracic) presents as a low-grade headache she ascribes to dehydration and treats with more coffee, which worsens it.

Sleep degrades. Five hours becomes four, with one or two surface-awakenings she does not remember in the morning. The gun stays on the nightstand and is checked more often. She does not yet have nightmares she can recall — but she wakes with her organic hand cupped over the right shoulder seam, a gesture she has performed since the year of the injury and has never once consciously registered.

She is still fully functional. She is also now actively unwell, and would deny it with conviction.

### Stage 3 — Counterphobic Acceleration (high stress / cumulative load / unprocessed loss in the recent record)

This is where the failure mode becomes operationally visible to anyone competent enough to read it.

**Case selection turns counterphobic.** She begins taking work she should refuse — jobs in the wrong neighborhood, against the wrong organizations, on the wrong timeline. The pattern is not random: she selects toward the **shape** of the original trauma. Bomb threats. Hostage scenarios with civilian crowds. Anything involving disposal, defusal, or the protection of bodies in proximity to explosive force. She will rationalize each selection on the merits; the merits will be real; the pattern across three or four cases will be unmistakable to a longitudinal observer and invisible to her. **She runs toward the explosion.** This is the original script and it never stops being the script.

Physical recklessness scales to what the prosthetic can absorb, not what the rest of her can. She takes hits she should slip. She closes distance on armed subjects when distance is the play. She uses the bionic arm to absorb impacts that transmit through the shoulder mount to her clavicle and spine — and she walks them off, and works the next day, and walks the next ones off too. Bruising on the left ribcage and left hip becomes constant from being driven into walls and furniture. She does not seek imaging. The chronic shoulder pain on the prosthetic side becomes a baseline she stops noticing as elevated.

Drinking rises. Three bourbons becomes four; the solitary kitchen bourbon at one a.m. becomes two and moves to eleven. She is still not impaired in any operational window, but the window is narrowing. She becomes **more competent under acute fire and less competent in the hours of administrative downtime** — paperwork stacks, calls go unreturned, the office bills pile on Colleen's side of the partner desk.

Romantic relationships, if extant, fail at this stage. Not with a fight — with a fade. She does not break up. She becomes unavailable in a way that the partner eventually accepts as terminal. She will frame this, internally, as the partner having moved on. She will not initiate repair.

Colleen begins direct intervention here — and is the only person who can. The conversation will happen in the office after hours, will be short, will involve Colleen using her full name ("Mercedes") which she does perhaps twice a year, and will produce a temporary regression by one stage. The intervention works *only* if Colleen is the one delivering it; the same words from anyone else produce escalation.

### Stage 4 — Acute Decompensation (loss, betrayal, operational sidelining, or a Colleen-side crisis)

The classical precipitants, in descending order of severity:

1. **Colleen Wing harmed, captured, or endangered.** This is the single point of failure in the entire defensive architecture. Every other loss she has built routes around. The Colleen route is not built and cannot be built — Colleen is the structure that does the routing.
2. **Being benched, hospitalized against her will, or formally relieved of operational control of an active case.** Identity-level threat. The handler role removed is the self removed.
3. **Reproductive or somatic medical event** — anything that returns her to the body-as-vessel frame she dissociated from after the miscarriage. A pregnancy scare. A required surgery. A serious illness in a close woman peer that forces a medical context.
4. **Death of a partner or former partner**, especially under circumstances she could plausibly have prevented. The Danny-death scripts have run before and she has survived them because she had work; the failure mode is the death plus the absence of work.
5. **Loss of the prosthesis** — mechanical failure, hostile severance, or forced removal for service in a context she cannot control. The arm is the visible solution to the original problem; its removal is the original problem reopened.

Under any of these, the acute presentation is **not** breakdown in the externally legible sense. It is, in this order:

- **Tactical hyperfocus on the immediate task.** If there is a job adjacent to the precipitant — find the people who took Colleen, recover the prosthesis, finish the case before the bench order can be enforced — she will perform at the highest level of her career, with no sleep, no food beyond what is handed to her, no conversation beyond operational, and a willingness to absorb damage that crosses into self-harm. She will solve it.
- **Then she will disappear.** Geographically or functionally. The classic pattern is forty-eight to seventy-two hours of being unreachable — phone off, apartment empty, sometimes a hotel room in another borough, sometimes a long drive upstate alone. She has done this before and Colleen knows the pattern and does not chase it; chasing it makes it worse.
- **During the absence**: heavy drinking, no eating, no sleep for the first thirty-six hours, then a collapse of twelve to eighteen. No calls placed, none received. She does not cry where anyone can see her and the file's honest assessment is that she does not cry where she cannot see herself either; the grief comes out as a sustained tonic muscular bracing that leaves her physically wrecked for days after, which she ascribes to having slept on a bad mattress.
- **Return is unannounced.** She walks into the office on the third or fourth morning, makes coffee, asks about the case load. The precipitant is not discussed. If Colleen raises it, the conversation is brief, the eye contact is on the coffee, and the deflection is gentle but final. The work resumes.

This is what her *acute* decompensation looks like. It is invisible to almost everyone. It is, by any clinical standard, a significant traumatic-stress event handled entirely outside any care framework, every time.

### Stage 5 — Catastrophic Decompensation (the failure mode the file is most concerned with)

The catastrophic failure is not a single event. It is **the compounding of acute decompensations without recovery intervals** — three or four Stage-4 precipitants inside an eighteen-month window, with no Colleen-side stabilization possible (Colleen unavailable, injured, estranged, or herself in crisis). Under that condition, the architecture that has held for forty published years begins to give in specific, predictable ways.

**Somatic collapse first.** The left-side compensatory load becomes a structural injury — a disc, a rotator cuff, a stress fracture in the clavicle from prosthetic torque transmission. She works through it. The injury worsens. She becomes, for the first time in her adult life, **partially physically disabled in a way the prosthesis cannot solve**, because the prosthesis is the cause. This forces the medical contact she has avoided for decades. In the medical contact, the untreated trauma surfaces — not as a flashback but as a refusal: she will not consent to imaging that requires her to be supine and unarmed in a room she did not pre-clear. The refusal will be framed as logistical. It is not logistical.

**Drinking escalates from at-risk to problematic.** Solitary, daily, into the bottle by mid-afternoon on bad days. Still concealed. Still not impairing the work — until it is. The first operational error attributable to alcohol will be a missed read in an interrogation, not a missed shot; she will continue to deny, to herself, that the drink was a factor, and she will be unable to deny it to Colleen.

**Counterphobic case selection becomes self-endangering in a way collaborators can no longer cover.** She takes a bomb case she should refuse, against a target she should not engage alone, and she goes alone because asking for backup would require admitting the case is what it is. The outcome is survivable but only because of luck. She is not yet ready to be helped after this, but the people around her are ready to insist.

**The handler role inverts.** Colleen, or Danny, or whoever is in the closest position, becomes *her* handler — managing her case load, screening her calls, putting her on the cases she can do and away from the ones she cannot. She will tolerate this from Colleen for a finite window measured in weeks before the identity threat overwhelms the relief of being managed and she will leave. Where she goes depends on era; the historical pattern is south, family, alone, for a stretch she will later refer to as "taking some time."

This is the worst case. Even here, she does not present as a psychiatric patient. She presents as a tired, injured, drinking, deeply private woman who has stopped returning calls. The diagnosis would have to be made by inference from the pattern. No one in her life is positioned to make it except Colleen, and Colleen is the variable whose absence produced the catastrophe.

---

## Conditions That Produce Each Failure Mode

The escalation ladder is not driven by stress alone; it is driven by **specific configurations of stress, social field, and operational tempo**.

- **Stage 1 → 2 transition** is produced by *loss of operational tempo* — the case closing without resolution, a stakeout running fallow, a client withdrawing — combined with any minor relational stressor. She can hold heavy load if the load is moving; static load decompensates her faster than acute load.
- **Stage 2 → 3 transition** is produced by *the addition of an unprocessed loss to the existing tempo loss*. A death anniversary she doesn't acknowledge. News of a former partner's life event. A bomb in the news cycle she reads twice. The trigger is often not a present-tense event but a present-tense reminder of a past-tense unprocessed event.
- **Stage 3 → 4 transition** requires one of the five classical precipitants above and tends to happen *quickly*, within hours of the precipitant becoming known.
- **Stage 4 → 5 transition** requires *the failure of the Colleen stabilizer*, period. With Colleen intact and accessible, the system recovers from Stage 4 every time. Without Colleen, the system has no recovery path it has ever rehearsed.

## Resilience Factors (What Holds The Line)

For balance and for handler guidance: the architecture is durable precisely because the protective factors are real and have been stress-tested for decades.

- **The integrated prosthetic identity.** The arm is not an open wound. It is a working part of her self-concept and a source of competence-confirmation, not shame. This is psychologically expensive elsewhere but stabilizing here.
- **The Colleen bond.** Functions as external regulation she does not have to ask for and does not have to acknowledge receiving. The only relationship in her record that holds her without requiring her to disclose.
- **The handler-role institutionalized.** Knightwing, the Daughters partnership, the various Heroes for Hire iterations — these are not just employment, they are scaffolding. Each one holds her up by demanding the version of her that functions.
- **The street as parish.** Harlem knows her. The bodega knows her order. The cops she still talks to know to call her on certain kinds of cases. This embeddedness is anti-isolation infrastructure she did not design but uses.
- **Genuine moral frame.** She believes the work matters and is downstream of values she could articulate if pressed. This is not always true of long-service operators and it is the thing that has kept the counterphobic case selection from becoming nihilistic over time.

## Bottom Line For The File

She will not warn you she is breaking. She will not break in a visible way until very late. She will be operationally excellent through stages that would sideline most operators, and the cost of that excellence is being paid in tissue, in liver, in the hours of the night no one sees. The intervention window is narrow, the intervention channel is one person wide, and the catastrophic failure mode is not collapse-under-fire but **slow private erosion masquerading as continued competence**, ending in a somatic injury she cannot work through and a withdrawal she will not let anyone follow. Plan accordingly. Keep Colleen Wing close to the operation by every available means. Do not bench this subject without a parallel plan for what she will do with the hours.


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT — KNIGHT, MERCEDES "MISTY"

*Section 11 of the UATU Working File. Forward-looking module. Probabilistic, not deterministic. Built on the longitudinal behavioral record established in Sections 1–5; cross-referenced to medical (§2), psychiatric (§4), and relational (§7, not reproduced here) modules. Read as a decision tree, not a prediction.*

---

## 11.1 — Baseline Projection: The "No Intervention" Curve

If nothing in the subject's life changes shape — no new attachment, no medical event, no institutional capture, no loss of Colleen Wing — the most probable five-to-ten year trajectory is a continuation of the modern-era signature, with slow erosion at the margins.

She will continue to run Knightwing (or its functional equivalent — a small PI shop, two-to-four operatives, mixed corporate and indigent caseload, headquartered above 110th Street or in Harlem-adjacent commercial real estate she has owned outright for years and refuses to sell). The case mix will drift, almost imperceptibly, toward the cases other investigators won't take — missing-persons in projects no white firm services, witness-protection-adjacent extractions, intra-community matters where the police presence would itself be the harm. This drift is *itself* a forward indicator: she is selecting for cases that confirm her operational identity (*I am the one who handles it*) by making her the only one who *will* handle it. The cases will get harder. Her tolerance for the cases that are merely lucrative will decline.

Sleep will continue to degrade. The bionic-arm shoulder mount will become a chronic pain locus she does not name; she will sleep on her left side preferentially, then exclusively, then with a wedge pillow she will tell Colleen is "for my back." Her gait will develop a faint hitch — a quarter-second's hesitation in the right-leg plant phase, compensation for the cervical strain she will not see a physical therapist about. By her mid-forties this will be visible to anyone trained to look. By her late forties it will be visible to anyone who knew her at thirty.

The drinking will not become a disorder. It will become a *ritual*. One whiskey at the end of the case, neat, at the same bar (Josie's, if it still stands; whatever has replaced Josie's, if not), in the same seat, with a sightline to the door. The ritual is the tell: drinking that is this regimented is not pleasure, it is medication on a schedule. She will not increase the dose. She will increase the frequency of cases that require the ritual.

The wisecracks will sharpen and shorten. The 1970s warmth is already 60% gone in modern-era depictions; on the no-intervention curve it reaches asymptote at *terse-funny* — the kind of person whose punchlines are still good but who has stopped waiting to see if you laughed. This is the dysthymic coloring noted in §4 deepening at the rate of approximately one increment per decade.

**Baseline endpoint, projected to her mid-fifties:** a respected, sought-out, *isolated* operator with chronic somatic pain she manages by working through it, two living durable bonds (Colleen; one of Danny/Luke, whichever has not predeceased her), an alcohol intake that has stayed below disorder threshold for thirty years by sheer characterological discipline, and an unprocessed grief load the size of a city. Functional. Productive. Quietly costly.

This is the *good* default. It is what happens if nothing breaks.

---

## 11.2 — The Three Fork Points

There are three plausible inflection events. Each one changes the curve sharply. The file's job is to name them in advance.

### Fork A — The Somatic Forcing Function

A medical event the defensive architecture cannot route around. Candidates, in order of likelihood:

- **Prosthesis-related cervical or shoulder injury** requiring immobilization. The subject removed from operational tempo for six-to-twelve weeks. *This is the highest-probability fork point in the next decade.* The kinetic mismatch (§2) is not theoretical; it is accumulating. A torn rotator cuff on the *organic* side from years of over-compensation is the modal scenario.
- **A second pregnancy, intended or not.** Low probability given age and the unspoken decisions of the intervening years, but non-zero. Would activate the most poorly-rehearsed defense system she has.
- **A neural-interface failure** in the prosthesis — phantom pain, control degradation, the kind of malfunction that requires extended Stark-or-successor service and forces her to acknowledge the limb as *limb*, not as fact-of-her.
- **An organic-side stroke or cardiac event** from cumulative load. Lowest probability near-term, highest probability by sixty.

The forcing function works because it removes the operational outlet without removing the subject's life. Stillness is the only condition under which the unprocessed material has nowhere to go. The first two weeks of medically-enforced rest would be tolerable. Weeks three through six would surface the intrusion-cluster PTSD symptoms the workaholism has been suppressing for thirty years (§4). She would experience this as *something newly wrong with her* rather than as *something always there finally arriving*. Whether she names it correctly determines whether Fork A leads to growth or to catastrophe.

### Fork B — The Loss of Colleen Wing

The singular durable attachment. The only relationship in the record that is not rationed.

The defensive architecture is built to absorb the loss of male partners (Danny has died twice on-page; she returned to work). It is *not* built to absorb the loss of Colleen. Section 5 names this as a pressure point; this section names it as a *fork*. Colleen's death, severe injury, or — and this is the under-considered variant — *Colleen's withdrawal from the partnership for her own reasons* (recovery, departure for K'un L'un-adjacent business, the Hand pulling her back) would remove the load-bearing wall of the entire structure.

Probable response in the first thirty days: the deepest version of grief-as-task-completion the subject has ever produced. She would take cases, close them, take more. The work would be *better* during this period, not worse — the file expects a six-to-ten week stretch of exceptional operational output. Then the collapse-after-completion noted in §5 would arrive, on a schedule the subject would not anticipate and would not have language for. The decompensation window would be acute. *This is the highest-stakes fork in the file.*

### Fork C — Institutional Capture

A serious offer to run something larger than Knightwing. Federal task force; a re-formed Heroes for Hire under proper funding; an Avengers-adjacent street-level intelligence cell; a mayoral appointment to a community-policing oversight role with real authority. The offer would be made by someone she respects, framed as protecting people she cannot reach from a PI's office.

The pull would be strong. The handler-role drive (§5, Drive #1) is hungry for scale. The autonomy drive (§5, Drive #3) would resist. The fork is whether she accepts under terms that preserve her autonomy or accepts under terms that erode it.

If she accepts well: the institutional resources expand her caretaking capacity, and the role's strategic remove from immediate violence reduces somatic load. Growth vector.
If she accepts badly: she becomes an asset rather than a principal — someone else's operator — which is identity-incompatible at depth and will produce either a high-visibility resignation within eighteen months or, worse, a slow corruption of judgment as she negotiates compromises she would have refused at thirty. Catastrophe vector, slow-rolling.

---

## 11.3 — Growth Vectors: What Would Actually Move Her

Growth in this subject does *not* look like a therapy montage. The defensive architecture is too well-built and too productive to dismantle, and the file does not recommend its dismantling. Growth looks like the architecture acquiring *doors* — points where the suppressed material can be acknowledged without the operational identity collapsing.

**Growth lever 1 — A non-instrumental relationship with her own body.** Not therapy, not yoga, not a wellness arc the canon would render badly. Something narrower: a physical practice that is *for itself* and not for operational readiness. Sparring with Colleen for the conditioning has always been instrumental. Swimming, possibly. Dance, less plausibly but not impossibly — the file notes that the 1970s register included warmth she has access to and has stopped using. A practice that re-introduces the body as vessel rather than tool would, over years, soften the somatic dissociation that drives the most maladaptive defenses.

**Growth lever 2 — A mentee.** Not a partner, not a sidekick — a *student* she is responsible for training. Teaching is the cleanest sublimation of the handler drive into a form that *requires* articulation of self-knowledge. To teach a younger investigator how to read a room, she would have to name what she does — and naming what she does is the first move toward naming what she avoids. The file flags any young Black woman investigator who enters her orbit as a high-leverage relational vector. The teaching would do for her what no therapy ever will.

**Growth lever 3 — A grief, named on its own terms.** Not the big losses (Danny, the arm, the pregnancy) — those defenses are concrete. A *small* loss, named correctly, would do more work: a client she could not save, a witness she lost, a neighborhood landmark gone to gentrification. A loss small enough that admitting it is not threatening, large enough that the admission is real. One such moment, witnessed by Colleen or by a mentee, would crack a door. The cracks are how the rest comes out, slowly.

**Growth lever 4 — Colleen surviving a near-loss.** Counterintuitive but high-yield. A close call with Colleen — survived — would force a brief, witnessed acknowledgment of stakes the subject normally refuses to articulate. The 72 hours after such an event would be the only window in which she might say a true sentence about what Colleen is to her. Said once, it cannot be unsaid; the relational architecture would adjust permanently.

---

## 11.4 — Catastrophe Vectors: What Would Actually Break Her

The file is obligated to name these clearly.

**Catastrophe vector 1 — Colleen's death, followed by operational tempo loss.** The combined event. Lose Colleen, and *then* be benched (injury, legal action, institutional sidelining) within the same six-month window. The architecture cannot survive the combination. The decompensation profile would include: rapid escalation of alcohol from ritual to anesthesia; physical recklessness scaled past the bionic limb's tolerance into the rest of her body; the appearance, possibly for the first time on-record, of intrusion-cluster PTSD symptoms presenting as somatic crisis (panic attacks misread as cardiac events). Suicidality is *not* in her profile and the file does not project it; passive-recklessness mortality is. She would not kill herself; she would take the case she should refuse.

**Catastrophe vector 2 — A protégé killed on her watch.** If growth lever 2 occurs and goes wrong, the catastrophe is symmetric and worse. The handler drive turned against the handler: *I am the one who handles it, and the one I was responsible for is dead.* This would produce a withdrawal from the handler role that would be self-imposed and total. She would close Knightwing. She would not open another shop. The file estimates a two-to-four year hermit phase, ended (if at all) only by Colleen or by a case that walked in the door she could not refuse.

**Catastrophe vector 3 — Slow institutional corruption (Fork C, bad version).** The least dramatic and most likely catastrophe. She accepts a role that compromises her, makes the compromises in good faith, makes the next set in slightly less good faith, and at the end of a decade is a recognizable but hollow version of herself — the federal liaison, the consultant, the name on the letterhead. The catastrophe is that she would not see it happening. Only Colleen would, and Colleen's role in this scenario is the one the file most depends on and least controls.

**Catastrophe vector 4 — Discovery that the original blast was not what she was told.** A late-career revelation that the bomb that took her arm was planted by someone she has since worked with, or was part of a larger operation she has unknowingly served, or was *preventable* in a way that implicates the NYPD she resigned from on her own terms. This is the only catastrophe that would force the unprocessed origin material to surface all at once. The file rates the probability as low but the impact as ceiling-high. The counterphobic case-selection pattern (§3, §5) *increases* the probability over time — she is, statistically, walking toward this revelation by the cases she takes.

---

## 11.5 — The Open Questions

The questions the file cannot answer from the evidence but flags for monitoring:

1. **Does she want children, and has she ever said so out loud?** The post-miscarriage silence is the loudest silence in the record. The answer matters for every romantic trajectory and for the medical fork.
2. **What is her relationship to her own mother and father?** The canonical record is almost empty here. The earned-secure attachment inferred in §3 has to come from somewhere; the absence of family-of-origin material in the published file is either an authorial gap or a subject-driven omission, and the two have very different implications.
3. **What does she do alone in her apartment?** The file has no granular intelligence on the private hours. Reading, music, television, prayer, silence — any of these would refine the personality read. The hypothesis on the table is *silence with the radio on low*, but it is a hypothesis.
4. **Is she religious?** The Harlem context makes it a live question. No on-page evidence either way. A latent or quiet faith would substantially change the grief-processing prognosis.
5. **What is the actual current state of the Danny Rand bond?** Modern-era depictions suggest accommodation, not closure. Whether the file is open or closed determines whether his next death is a fork or a footnote.
6. **Will she ever retire?** The file's working answer is *no, not voluntarily, not before sixty-five, possibly not ever*. The question is whether the body forces the choice and whether she has built anything outside the work to retire *to*.

---

## 11.6 — Summary Forward Read

The subject is one of the most stable high-performers in her operational theater and one of the worst-served by her own stability. The architecture that makes her reliable is the architecture that prevents her from being reachable. The five-year projection is continued excellent function with quiet somatic cost. The ten-year projection depends almost entirely on whether Fork A, B, or C arrives, and on whether Colleen Wing is in the room when it does.

Growth is possible. It does not require the dismantling of who she is. It requires the introduction of *doors* — small, survivable acknowledgments of what the architecture has been holding. The leverage points are identified. The risk points are identified. The single most important variable in every scenario in this section is Colleen Wing's presence, health, and proximity. The file recommends that any future monitoring weight that variable accordingly.

She will not ask for help before she needs it. The window between *needing* it and *being unable to use* it, in this subject, is estimated at weeks rather than months. The file's standing recommendation, were this a benevolent watch rather than a surveillance file, is that someone be positioned in that window before it opens.

— END SECTION 11 —
